That's really the point of typical allergies. The reason you develop them (the common kinds, like peanuts) is because you were never used to them; for example, peanut allergies are higher in children/cultures where they don't get a taste of it early on. So you can build your immunity towards it little by little (at least on the mundane allergies).

Sometimes your body can adjust to the allergy and tolerate it. I've lived with cats all my life and didn't think I was allergic. But when I migrated to another country I didn't have a cat for 8 years until finally it was time to get a cat. Lo and behold, my cat almost killed me. Really bad allergic reaction, and I locked myself in a room for days and weeks. But as time went by I started having less and less reaction to the cat. It's been 7 years with the same cat and I'd still get reactions once in a while but very rarely these days.  And my allergy doctor confirmed that I am indeed allergic to cats.  One key thing, give the cats frequent baths.

As a tip, don't go to Banff. Or at the very least avoid staying there! Stay in Canmore instead! I'm not biased or anything because I grew up and also currently live in Canmore, and my dad runs a resort in Canmore... But it's only 30 minutes away from Banff, it's cheaper, and you're still surrounded by mountains with way less people around. You'll get better resorts out here that are a lot bigger and nicer then your standard hotel unless if you plan on staying at the fairmont resort (which is nice but kinda old). There's also a bus that goes to Banff from Canmore if you don't want to drive and honestly it's cheaper then driving and paying for parking in Banff (if you manage to find a spot). Seriously, you'll only want to actually be in Banff for one or two days before you'll want nothing to do with it. Also avoid the summer like the plague and come around the end of September. It will still be warm but if you're lucky you'll get the beautiful fall colours, and there is nothing like it seeing the mountains during the 1 week of fall that we get! Drumheller is also absolutely gorgeous at that time of the year too!  This is just some general advice btw, not just for Chris ğŸ˜‚.

I don't know if anyone is interested in hearing this but I think it depends on the breed when you are allergic to animals. I am allergic to rats but not all of them. Still can't risk getting anymore pet rats. I am not allergic to the cat I have but I would sneeze like crazy with some of other people's cars. Must have something to do with the fur or what they carrying around on it. Animals have allergies too. My cat has food allergies and I used to have a rat that had skin allergy to ducted heating. It is true that some allergies go away over time or your immune system stops reacting to it. My son was born with peanut and egg allergies and I was advised to slowly introduce tiny amounts of eggs over the years to help his body build resistance. Children hospital research shows that you as a kid have 20 percent chance to outgrow peanut allergy and 70 percent chance to outgrow egg allergy. There is still no answer to why people have allergies in the first place. Same with rheumatoid arthritis. The immune system is complicated.

My partner used to be allergic to cats. Some cats either produce less of the most common enzyme people react to, some breeds are known for that like the Rex breeds and Bengals like I have, or your body really just gets used to it through exposure. Pretty much how immunization would work if you went to a doctor for a cat allergy just with more cuddles and less shots and meds. That's how it worked with my partner, cuddling with our first Bengal who does produce significantly less of that enzyme slowly showed his body that there is nothing to freak out over. Then we got a second Bengal and his last allergy test basically showed no reaction anymore. Even the doctor was surprised how much his allergy has reduced. Which is great for my partner because now he can cuddle all of the cats he meets. Especially at his job as an electrician for a rental company.

Ok, only kinda on topic, but the "no showers" thing: You should not wash your hair everyday because it strips all the oils from your hair, making it more oily over time. It takes a bit of time at first since your body thinks it needs to produce more oil but after a little while your body will adjust and you will not need to wash your hair as much. Of course you should still shower/bathe everyday just don't wash your hair every time (wear a shower cap or something to keep it dry).
